(B) **`/api/geo/waitlist contract (probe-only, safe)`** вЂ” 6 assertions across 4 safe probes: invalid country `"ZZ"` в†’ 400 `country_not_eligible`; `consent: false` в†’ 400 `consent_required` (pins the `z.literal(true)` error-map from Zod); malformed JSON body в†’ 400 `invalid_json` (pins the `try { await req.json() } catch` early-reject branch so a refactor that drops the guard fails here); GET в†’ 405 (pins the POST-only contract). **Probe safety design**: every probe constructs a payload where every OTHER Zod check passes, so `parsed.error.issues[0]` is deterministic. Zod runs validation BEFORE the DB insert, so no rows are ever created from these probes вЂ” safe to run against prod on every push. Rate-limit Maps are never touched for the same reason (rate-limit check runs after Zod). (C) **`/api/auth/providers (NextAuth configuration surface)`** вЂ” 3 assertions: endpoint returns 200 JSON (proves `[...nextauth]` catch-all is wired); response includes `google` provider with `id === "google"`; `callbackUrl` starts with `https://pdfcraftai.com/` (apex, NOT `www.pdfcraftai.com`). The apex-vs-www pin is deliberate вЂ” `www` 308-redirects to apex, breaks OAuth's exact-URL-match validation, and this exact bug ate an afternoon during initial OAuth setup. A future `NEXTAUTH_URL` env-var drift now fails smoke before it gets attributed to Google Console instead of infrastructure. (D) **AI tool runners** вЂ” grew from 6 to 10 probed paths. ai-rewrite (3cr), ai-table (3cr), ai-generate (20cr), ai-sign (10cr) were added to `lib/tools.ts` but never back-filled into the smoke harness; the "tool page 404s after a data-only edit" regression class is now caught end-to-end. **Offline test gate still green**: `npm test` unchanged at 390/390 across 4 suites in 0.7вЂ“0.9s (pdf-tools 17 + geo-router 148 + geo-waitlist 217 + dev-hooks 8 вЂ” smoke isn't part of the offline gate by design, it hits real HTTPS and needs network access). **Blocker narrative**: first verification run of the extended harness against prod returned 62 failures because Hostinger had stuck on a post-deploy 503 (classic CLAUDE.md В§5 gotcha вЂ” new code pulled + runtime not re-started). SSH-based restart attempts hit "Connection closed by remote host" twice, likely Hostinger's SSH abuse throttling. 503 self-cleared within ~20 min (presumably via Hostinger's process supervisor finally killing the stuck worker). Re-ran `npm run smoke` against apex: **74/74 green**, proving the extension is correct AND Hostinger is healthy. Zero code changes to the smoke harness between the two runs вЂ” the 503 was infrastructural, not a harness bug. **Post-push 503 + SSH-based worker restart playbook** (added as follow-up knowledge): the deploy that landed this commit (`c11bef3` + docs backfill `44566d4`) triggered Hostinger's auto-pull as expected, but immediately bounced back to 503 for the second time today. SSH to `u692382124@212.85.28.206:65002` revealed `ps aux | grep next-server` listing **10 concurrent stale `next-server (v14.2.35)` processes** spanning start times 07:40 в†’ 08:17, with `bash: fork: retry: Resource temporarily unavailable` on every shell command вЂ” the process-table-exhaustion signature that causes the 503 to surface to Cloudflare. Root-cause inferred: Hostinger's managed Node supervisor spawns a new worker on every code-push redeploy but fails to reap the prior ones under certain conditions (possibly when the previous deploy was itself restarting from a 503 state вЂ” a cascade failure rather than a single stuck worker). **Remediation**: `ssh ... 'pkill -f "next-server"'` killed all 10 stale workers; supervisor respawned one clean worker within ~15s; `/api/health` flipped from 503 в†’ 200 with `"uptimeSec":1`; `npm run smoke` re-ran 74/74 green against the fresh worker. This is a lower-friction alternative to the hPanel "Stop running process" button documented in CLAUDE.md В§5 вЂ” SSH + `pkill` is one shell command; hPanel is a browser round-trip through Hostinger's UI. **Follow-up to capture in CLAUDE.md В§5**: "If SSH is available and you see > 3 concurrent `next-server` processes in `ps aux`, `pkill -f next-server` is the fastest unstick path. If SSH is throttled (seen earlier today, got "Connection closed by remote host" twice), fall back to hPanel." (2026-04-21)
- [x] **Tracked pre-push hook via `.githooks/` + `core.hooksPath` bootstrap** (commit `ef781ba`). Dev-hygiene infrastructure that turns the `npm test` gate (shipped in `01b0eaa`) into an automatic pre-push check вЂ” catches regressions BEFORE they hit GitHub Actions CI (let alone Hostinger's auto-deploy-on-push behaviour). Four files in one commit: (1) `.githooks/pre-push` NEW (100 lines, `#!/usr/bin/env bash` + `set -euo pipefail`) вЂ” runs `npm test` before any `git push`, exits non-zero on failure to abort the push, documents two bypass paths (`git push --no-verify` AND `GIT_PRE_PUSH_SKIP_TESTS=1 git push` вЂ” the env var is more greppable in shell history, the flag is built-in and requires no config). Logs what it's doing with prefixed output so it's clear this is the hook, not the test runner, if something goes sideways. (2) `.githooks/README.md` NEW вЂ” 25-line explainer on the `core.hooksPath` convention (tracked hook directory vs. the untracked `.git/hooks/` default), the one-command install (`git config core.hooksPath .githooks`), a short bullet per hook in the directory. (3) `docs/DEV_SETUP.md` NEW (140 lines) вЂ” full developer onboarding: prerequisites (Node в‰Ґ 18.17.0; both 18 and 20 tested in CI; 22 works locally but not production-pinned on Hostinger), first-run setup (`npm ci` в†’ opt into `.githooks` в†’ `npm test` verify), deep dive on what `core.hooksPath` does and why it's used over the default `.git/hooks/`, expected pre-push output with the 2026-04-21 snapshot of `382 passed, 0 failed across 3 suites` (intentionally pre-dev-hooks-suite to match the runner behaviour at hook install time, since adding the 8th dev-hooks assertion landed separately in `24709789261` CI-verification work), bypass paths with legitimate-reason examples (test-expectation diff atomically committed; docs-only branch while unrelated tests are broken on main; work-in-progress rebase flow), standalone harness invocations, CI + deploy flow context, troubleshooting (push hangs в†’ suspect `npm test` drift; hook fires on tag push в†’ expected behaviour, use `--no-verify origin <tag>`; permanently disable в†’ `git config --unset core.hooksPath`). (4) `scripts/test-dev-hooks.mjs` NEW вЂ” 8-assertion test harness that pins the hook's contract so a future refactor can't silently break the local gate: hook file exists; user-executable bit is set (`mode & 0o100`); shebang matches `/^#!\/(usr\/)?(bin\/)?(env\s+)?(bash|sh)\b/` (cross-platform POSIX-shell compat); hook body calls `npm test` (verbatim regex `\bnpm\s+test\b`); hook documents at least one bypass path (`--no-verify` OR `GIT_PRE_PUSH_SKIP_TESTS`); `.githooks/README.md` references the install command; `docs/DEV_SETUP.md` references the install command AND documents the bypass. Harness was added to `scripts/run-all-tests.mjs`'s `SUITES` array as the 4th and final suite вЂ” placed last because it's a self-consistency gate on the repo's own dev tooling (if someone strips the executable bit off the hook or rewires it to call something other than `npm test`, this fails here rather than silently at push time). Runner output now shows `[OK  ] dev-hooks         8 passed,  0 failed` alongside the three subsystem gates; total 390 assertions, ~0.7s wall-clock, unchanged semantics of the top-level `npm test` command. Zero runtime dependencies (stdlib-only: `node:fs` + `node:path` + `node:url`), consistent with the rest of the harness fleet. **Why this is additive rather than Task-critical**: same framing as the runner + CI + smoke-alias trilogy above вЂ” the pre-push hook is dev-hygiene infrastructure that compounds. GitHub Actions CI already runs `npm test` on every push to `main` and every PR, so a regression would eventually get caught. But catching it locally before the push saves the round-trip to CI + the "did I just break main for 3 minutes" anxiety, and the hook costs 0.7s. With the `dev-hooks` self-pin, a future refactor that breaks the hook's contract (renames `.githooks/pre-push`, strips the x-bit, swaps `npm test` for a specific harness, or drops the bypass documentation) fails `npm test` itself вЂ” the gate detects drift in its own gate. **Intentionally NOT done today**: a commit-msg hook to enforce conventional-commit prefixes (design call on style posture, punt until we've shipped a few more multi-author weeks); a pre-commit hook that runs typecheck (8s runtime вЂ” too slow for per-commit; stays as a manual / CI gate). (2026-04-21)
- [x] **Defensive audit: `Buffer.from` Г— pdf-lib intersection across the codebase вЂ” byteOffset bug confirmed isolated to test fixture** (commit `2f5d3ab`, docs-only). After the `ff507c7` fix, spent ~10 minutes confirming the Node-version-dependent Buffer.byteOffset bug couldn't bite us anywhere else. Audit method: three-stage grep narrowing. (1) Base64 decoder intersection вЂ” `rg -n "Buffer\.from\([^)]*['\"]base64['\"]"` across non-node_modules returned 2 hits, both already accounted for (this `docs/STATUS.md` paper trail + `scripts/test-pdf-tools.mjs` which was the bug). (2) Full Buffer.from consumer set вЂ” broadened to any `Buffer.from(` call: 15 files. (3) pdf-lib consumer set вЂ” grep for `from ['\"]pdf-lib['\"]` or `@cantoo/pdf-lib`: 29 files. Intersected (1)в€©(3) by file path в†’ 5 files in the risk surface: `app/api/ai/generate/route.ts`, `app/api/ai/redact/route.ts`, `app/api/ai/sign/route.ts`, `lib/ai/ocr.ts`, `app/api/ai/ocr/route.ts`. Audited each for the specific dangerous pattern (Buffer в†’ pdf-lib image-embedding call). Findings per file: (a) **`app/api/ai/generate/route.ts`** вЂ” 3 `Buffer.from` callsites: line 225 is `sha256Hex(Buffer.from(markdown, "utf8"))` (UTF-8 text for hashing, terminal вЂ” sha256 hex output never flows into pdf-lib); lines 263 and 282 are `Buffer.from(result.pdfBytes).toString("base64")` (pdf-lib's OUTPUT being serialized back to base64 for the HTTP response вЂ” flow direction is OUT of pdf-lib, not IN). **Safe.** (b) **`app/api/ai/redact/route.ts`** вЂ” 3 callsites, same three patterns as generate (line 221 UTF-8 sha256, lines 259 + 277 pdf-lib output serialization). **Safe.** (c) **`app/api/ai/sign/route.ts`** вЂ” 3 callsites, same three patterns (line 253 UTF-8 sha256, lines 291 + 309 pdf-lib output serialization). **Safe.** (d) **`lib/ai/ocr.ts`** вЂ” 1 callsite at line 279: `Buffer.from(bytes).toString("base64")` is a terminal Uint8Array в†’ base64 polyfill for the Node runtime (where `btoa` doesn't accept byte arrays). Buffer is immediately consumed by `.toString` and discarded; never flows into pdf-lib. **Safe.** (e) **`app/api/ai/ocr/route.ts`** вЂ” 1 callsite at line 206: `sha256Hex(Buffer.from(result.markdown, "utf8"))` (UTF-8 text в†’ sha256). **Safe.** **Conclusion:** the five intersection files all use `Buffer.from` exclusively for one of two non-dangerous patterns вЂ” UTF-8 text for hashing/encoding, or pdf-lib OUTPUT serialization to base64 for HTTP responses. No callsite feeds a Node `Buffer` INTO pdf-lib's image embedders (`embedJpg` / `embedPng`). Production image-embed path (`components/tools/ImageToPdfTool.tsx:146`, separately confirmed in the `ff507c7` fix) uses `new Uint8Array(await file.arrayBuffer())` which gets a fresh byteOffset-0 ArrayBuffer from the File API. The byteOffset bug class is isolated to the two base64-decoded test fixtures that were fixed in `ff507c7`. **What would flag a future regression:** any new callsite shaped `embedJpg(Buffer.from(...))` or `embedPng(Buffer.from(...))` would reintroduce the bug on Node 18/20 runners. Docstrings on `makeRedPng` + `makeBlueJpg` in `scripts/test-pdf-tools.mjs` already explain the trap for future readers. A lint rule (`no-restricted-syntax` against `CallExpression[callee.property.name=/^embed(Jpg|Png)$/] > CallExpression[callee.object.name="Buffer"]`) would catch it mechanically вЂ” captured as follow-up idea when the lint-posture decision gets made (ESLint is installed but no `.eslintrc.json` exists yet, and adopting a posture is a design call not a rubber-stamp). (2026-04-21)
- [x] **pdf-lib byteOffset test-fixture bug caught by first CI run and fixed** (commit `ff507c7`). The brand-new CI workflow's first run (`24709613573`, on commit `8c9207b`) failed on both Node 18 and Node 20 with two pdf-tools assertions red: `embed a JPG as a single page` and `embed PNG + JPG as two pages in US Letter`, both with `Error: SOI not found in JPEG`. Same commit was 382/382 green in the sandbox on Node 22 вЂ” classic environment-dependent failure, exactly what CI exists to catch. Root cause: `pdf-lib@1.17.1` `cjs/core/embedders/JpegEmbedder.js:37` does `new DataView(imageData.buffer); dataView.getUint16(0)` to read the JPEG Start-of-Image marker. It reads at offset 0 of the underlying `ArrayBuffer`, NOT at `imageData.byteOffset`. When the fixture is a Node `Buffer` returned by `Buffer.from(base64, 'base64')`, that Buffer is backed by Node's shared slab allocator вЂ” `buf.byteOffset` can be nonzero, in which case the SOI read pulls two bytes of unrelated slab memory instead of the JPEG header. Node 22's slab layout happens to place tiny Buffers at offset 0 (sandbox passed); Node 18/20 runners don't (CI failed). Fix: switch `makeRedPng` and `makeBlueJpg` in `scripts/test-pdf-tools.mjs` from returning `Buffer.from(base64, 'base64')` to returning `Uint8Array.from(Buffer.from(base64, 'base64'))`. `Uint8Array.from(iterable)` iterates and copies bytes into a brand-new `ArrayBuffer`, so `byteOffset === 0` is guaranteed on every Node version. Verified locally (382/382 still green on Node 22) and via CI verification run `24709789261` (both `test (Node 18)` and `test (Node 20)` green). **Production safety**: grep'd for `embedJpg|embedPng` across the codebase вЂ” only `components/tools/ImageToPdfTool.tsx:146` uses them at runtime, and it already does `const bytes = new Uint8Array(await item.file.arrayBuffer())` before calling `embedJpg`. The File API gives a fresh byteOffset-0 ArrayBuffer, so production was never affected вЂ” the bug is isolated to the base64-decoded test fixtures. Docstrings added on both `makeRedPng` and `makeBlueJpg` explaining the bug so a future refactor that reaches for `Buffer.from` "because it's shorter" gets stopped at review. **This outcome validates the CI investment**: the workflow was shipped 15 minutes earlier as dev-hygiene infrastructure and paid for itself on its first run by catching a latent environment-dependent bug that had been silently sitting in the test harness. If a future Paddle/geo integration test hits the same Buffer pattern, the fix is now documented and the muscle memory is there to reach for `Uint8Array.from(вЂ¦)` instead. (2026-04-21)
- [x] **GitHub Actions CI workflow вЂ” automates the `npm test` gate** (commit `8c9207b` CI wiring + commit `ff507c7` immediate-regression-fix, verification run `24709789261` green on both Node 18 and Node 20). Direct follow-up to the `npm test` runner (commit `01b0eaa`): having a single-command gate is only half the value; the other half is running that gate automatically on every push so regressions get caught at PR time, not at Hostinger-redeploy time. New file `.github/workflows/ci.yml` runs `npm run typecheck` + `npm test` on every push to `main` and every PR targeting `main`, matrixed across Node 18 and Node 20. Key design choices embedded in the file header: (1) Matrix on 18 + 20 (both LTS, both within `engines.node: ">=18.17.0"`) вЂ” Hostinger's managed Node version has drifted across this account's history so locking CI to a single version would let a Hostinger Node bump silently pass CI on a version we don't actually ship. Node 22 intentionally NOT in the matrix вЂ” fine locally but not production-pinned on Hostinger. (2) `npm ci` (not `npm install`) for determinism вЂ” uses `package-lock.json` exactly, fails fast if lock is out of sync with `package.json`. (3) Cache `~/.npm` keyed on `package-lock.json` via `actions/setup-node@v4`'s built-in `cache: npm` вЂ” subsequent runs on the same lock skip the registry roundtrip. (4) Gates in order: typecheck first (fast, catches most drift), tests second (382 offline assertions, ~0.8s). (5) `next build` intentionally NOT a gate yet вЂ” some routes hit runtime integrations (DB adapter, NextAuth providers) at build time and would need the full secrets surface to succeed in CI; adding build coverage would require either stubbing those env vars or refactoring the routes (scope-creep for a first CI pass). typecheck catches the TS side of build errors; runtime-only build errors still surface at Hostinger deploy time, but Hostinger's auto-pull-on-push behaviour means CI is the last line of defence before production. (6) Concurrency group `ci-${{ github.ref }}` with `cancel-in-progress: ${{ github.ref != 'refs/heads/main' }}` вЂ” PR branches cancel superseded runs (saves Actions minutes when someone pushes three times in two minutes), but `main` pushes always run to completion so every main commit has a tracked verdict (critical because Hostinger auto-deploys every main push). (7) Zero secrets needed вЂ” both gates are pure-logic and offline. Verified locally both gates are green before first CI run (382/382 passing, typecheck clean) so the first workflow run will be a known-green baseline rather than a surprise red. Uses the PAT's already-granted `workflow` scope (`CLAUDE.md` В§2a confirms `repo`, `workflow`, `read:network_configurations`). **Intentionally NOT done today**: smoke-live.mjs in CI (would hit real production on every PR вЂ” noisy and unnecessary; `npm run smoke` stays a manual verb); lint gate (`eslint` is installed but not wired to `npm run lint` as a gate вЂ” `next lint` is the existing script, easy follow-up but needs a separate decision on which rules are CI-blocking); pre-commit hook (design choice between husky + git hook vs plain shell snippet in CONTRIBUTING.md вЂ” punt until the third additive hook request). **Why this is additive rather than Task-critical**: same framing as the runner itself вЂ” it's dev-hygiene infrastructure that compounds, not an unblocker for Task #1/#2/#3. But with `npm test` as the canonical gate already shipped, wiring CI is the 10-minute follow-up that turns "you can run the gate" into "the gate runs itself on every push", which is worth a lot more than the marginal 10 minutes. (2026-04-21)
- [x] **`npm run smoke` alias for the live-prod harness вЂ” follow-up to the `npm test` work** (commit `d4b336d`). `scripts/smoke-live.mjs` already shipped (dated paper-trail in `docs/E2E_SMOKE_2026-04-20.md` and `docs/FEATURE_TRACKER.md` line 122), but it was only runnable by path. Adding `"smoke": "node scripts/smoke-live.mjs"` to `package.json` gives the live-prod harness the same verb-first discoverability as `npm test`. Kept deliberately separate from `npm test` because smoke-live hits real production over HTTPS (`https://pdfcraftai.com` by default, `SMOKE_BASE` env-overridable) and assumes network access, whereas `npm test` is the offline pure-logic gate that must stay runnable in a sandbox or pre-push hook. Semantics: `npm test` = "does the repo's own logic pass?", `npm run smoke` = "is the deployed site healthy?" вЂ” distinct questions, distinct commands, both now one-verb invocations. One-line change to `package.json`; no functional delta to the harness itself; historical dated references to `node scripts/smoke-live.mjs` in `docs/E2E_SMOKE_2026-04-20.md` and `docs/FEATURE_TRACKER.md` are intentionally left unchanged because they describe a moment in time. Verified via `npm run` listing вЂ” alias registers alongside `test`. (2026-04-21)
- [x] **Unified `npm test` runner вЂ” dev-hygiene infrastructure** (commit `01b0eaa`). Task #3 has generated three standalone `scripts/test-*.mjs` harnesses (`test-pdf-tools.mjs`, 17 assertions; `test-geo-router.mjs`, 148 assertions; `test-geo-waitlist.mjs`, 217 assertions вЂ” 382 total). They share the plain-Node `assert()` + `pass`/`fail` counter idiom but each stands alone вЂ” no Jest/Vitest driver, no `"test"` script in `package.json`. Practical consequence: developers (and future Claude sessions) had to remember the full chain `node scripts/test-pdf-tools.mjs && node scripts/test-geo-router.mjs && node scripts/test-geo-waitlist.mjs` by hand, CI (when it lands) would have no canonical entrypoint, and there was no single "is the repo green?" command for pre-push sanity checks. Fix: new `scripts/run-all-tests.mjs` orchestrator + `"test": "node scripts/run-all-tests.mjs"` wired into `package.json`. Two files in one commit: (1) `scripts/run-all-tests.mjs` NEW вЂ” spawns each harness as a child process in declared order (pdf-tools в†’ geo-router в†’ geo-waitlist, chosen so the crypto-path suite fails first if a `pdf-lib` / `@cantoo/pdf-lib` dependency upgrade breaks decryption, rather than being masked by pure-logic noise later), pipes stdout/stderr to the parent in real time (dev sees output as it happens), ALSO buffers stdout so it can regex the summary-line tail `(\d+)\s+passed,\s+(\d+)\s+failed` out of each once the child closes, then prints an aggregated summary block showing `[OK  ]` / `[FAIL]` per suite + overall `N passed, M failed across K suites (T.Ts)` + overall `Result: PASS|FAIL`. Exits 1 if any suite failed to parse OR had failed assertions OR exited non-zero вЂ” "couldn't tell" is treated as a failure, which catches the case where a harness crashes before emitting its summary line. Zero runtime dependencies (stdlib only вЂ” `node:child_process` + `node:path` + `node:url`), matching the harnesses' own posture: keeps `npm test` fast and offline-safe. Adding a fourth harness is a three-step process documented in the file header (drop it in `scripts/`, make sure it ends with `N passed, M failed`, add one line to the `SUITES` array). Regex anchors on the common tail only, so future harnesses can prefix however they want ("Foo tests: 3 passed, 0 failed.", "3 passed, 0 failed.", etc.). (2) `package.json` MODIFIED вЂ” one line: `"test": "node scripts/run-all-tests.mjs"` inserted between `"typecheck"` and `"db:generate"`. Verified both directions: happy path `npm test` exits 0 with `382 passed, 0 failed across 3 suites`; failure path exercised via an ad-hoc synthetic harness that printed `0 passed, 1 failed` and exited 1 вЂ” aggregate exit was 1 as expected, so the "any suite red в†’ overall red" contract holds. Wall-clock runtime of the full suite: 0.8s, so `npm test` is cheap enough to put in front of every push without friction. **Why this is additive rather than Task #3-critical**: Task #3's two remaining sub-items (1c Cloudflare rule application; 2b `routeCheckoutByCountry` wiring into `createCheckoutAction`) are both externally blocked вЂ” 1c needs the user at the Cloudflare dashboard, 2b needs Paddle sandbox keys from Task #1. But each of the three test harnesses was born of Task #3 work, and the lack of a unified entrypoint is a paper-cut that gets worse with every additional subsystem the task generates. Fixing it now means the next sub-item to land (whether that's the Paddle integration tests when keys arrive or additional geo-policy coverage) drops into a repo that already has `npm test` as the canonical gate. (2026-04-21)

- [x] **`scripts/test-pdf-tools.mjs` вЂ” Node-based smoke harness for every client-side PDF tool.** Drives the same `pdf-lib` / `@cantoo/pdf-lib` APIs the browser runners use, so correctness can be asserted without a real browser. 17 tests across 7 tool groups: merge (3+2+4 pages, single-PDF passthrough), split (5-page в†’ 5 singletons), rotate & reorder (rotate, reverse, delete), compress (useObjectStreams resave stays valid), page numbers + watermark (stamp every page, diagonal overlay), image в†’ pdf (PNG, JPG, combined), protect + unlock (encrypt adds Encrypt dict, stock pdf-lib rejects, wrong password throws, user + owner password both unlock, resave strips encryption). All 17 pass in `node scripts/test-pdf-tools.mjs`. (2026-04-20)
- [x] **`scripts/smoke-live.mjs` вЂ” Production smoke harness.** Hits the live apex and asserts `/api/health` 200 + cache-control, GET 200 on 6 marketing pages + 7 tool runners, auth redirects for unauthed app routes, `/api/auth/forgot-password` contract (400 on bad email, 200 on valid вЂ” including replay, enforcing the anti-enumeration contract), `/api/auth/reset-password` contract (400 on missing / non-hex, 409 on unknown token), `/sitemap.xml` + `/robots.txt`. 24/26 pass as of 2026-04-20 02:45 UTC; the two failures (`/account` 404, unknown-token 500 on reset-password) are fixed locally and pending deploy вЂ” see "Prod hotfixes landing in next deploy" below. (2026-04-20)

### Prod hotfixes landing in next deploy

- [x] **Schema drift sweep вЂ” migration `0004_geo_waitlist.sql` backfilled in prod (DB-only, no code change, 2026-04-22).** Cross-checked every migration in `db/migrations/` against the live MariaDB 11.8.6 (`u692382124_pdfcraftai`) via SSH + the app credential. Result: 22 tables live, every column from 0005вЂ“0016 verified present (Tier-2 enrichment + net-margin + financials + billing-profile cols all there; `user_rate_limits` FK correctly references pluralized `users`, errno-150 repair from CLAUDE.md В§6 confirmed live). Two gaps surfaced: (a) `geo_waitlist` table from migration 0004 had never been applied вЂ” `SHOW TABLES LIKE 'geo_waitlist'` returned empty. Applied via `mysql --defaults-extra-file=...` from inside Hostinger using the app credential; post-state `SHOW CREATE TABLE` confirms PRIMARY KEY (id), UNIQUE (email,country), KEY country, KEY created_at all present, ENGINE=InnoDB CHARSET=utf8mb4. Tier-2 deferred-region waitlist signups (EU27/EEA/CH/CN/RU/BY per `docs/GEO_LAUNCH_POLICY.md`) now have somewhere to land. (b) **Logged as Task #28 backlog** вЂ” no Drizzle migration journal table in prod (`__drizzle_migrations`/`__journal` both absent), which is exactly why 0004 sat unapplied undetected for ~13 commits. See Task #28 below for the two candidate fixes. **No deploy / no commit needed for the table backfill itself** вЂ” pure DDL applied directly against the prod DB. (2026-04-22)
- [x] **Razorpay checkout: `publicConfig.keyId` в†’ `key` rename (commit `cb41e14`, 2026-04-22).** Paying user clicked **Buy pack** and got *"Payment Failed because of a configuration error. Authentication key was missing during initialization"* from the Razorpay hosted modal. Server-side order-creation was fine (`POST /orders` returned a fresh order id with the correct `RAZORPAY_KEY_ID`), so the API credentials weren't the problem вЂ” the failure was a property-name drift between `lib/payments/adapters/razorpay.ts:createOrder` (writing `publicConfig: { keyId: this.config.keyId, вЂ¦ }`) and `components/billing/CheckoutButton.tsx:launchCheckout` (reading `new Razorpay({ key: session.publicConfig.key, вЂ¦ })`). TypeScript couldn't see it because `CheckoutSession.publicConfig: Record<string, string>` is loosely typed (the union has to absorb Paddle's `clientToken/environment/sellerId` shape too). Fix renames the wire field on the adapter side to match what `checkout.js` actually reads, and preserves the env chain (`process.env.RAZORPAY_KEY_ID` в†’ `this.config.keyId` в†’ `publicConfig.key`). New `scripts/test-razorpay-handoff.mjs` (7 assertions across 3 sections вЂ” A adapter field names: writes `key:`, no `keyId:`, still sources from `this.config.keyId`; B client field reads: reads `.key`, never `.keyId`; C supporting fields: name + description with safe fallbacks) static-regex-pins the contract so the drift can't re-enter main. Aggregator post-change: 2645 passed / 0 failed across 27 suites; `npx tsc --noEmit` exit 0. Pushed to main 2026-04-22; Hostinger auto-deploy ~2вЂ“3 min. (2026-04-22)
- [x] **Admin allowlist: Gmail `+suffix` normalization (commit `13e1d29`, 2026-04-22).** `/admin` was 404'ing for every real founder session because `requireAdmin()` в†’ `notFound()` (anti-enumeration posture) and the founder-fallback was an exact-string `Set.has()` lookup against the allowlist. Diagnosed via `users.email` audit: 5 of 6 rows in prod are `+1`/`+2`/`+5`/`+razaorpay` aliases of `rajasekarjavaee@gmail.com` (Google collapses `+suffix` at delivery, so all those messages land in one inbox; NextAuth treats each variant as a distinct identity row keyed by the literal email Google returns in the OIDC token). Fix introduces `normalizeAdminEmail(email)` in `lib/admin/allowlist.ts` that вЂ” narrowly Gmail-scoped (`@gmail.com`/`@googlemail.com` only, because Outlook/Fastmail/etc. treat `+suffix` as a literal address) вЂ” slices off everything from `+` to the `lastIndexOf('@')` and lowercases the result. Both `parseAdminEmails` (env-allowlist parsing) and `isAdminEmail` (per-request check) route through it, and `parseAdminEmails` `.map(normalizeAdminEmail)` chain ensures literal allowlist entries are also folded. `requireAdmin()` в†’ `notFound()` surface is preserved вЂ” only the comparator changed. `scripts/test-admin-margin.mjs` SECTION E1 regex updated; new SECTION E2 (5 pins) covers helper export, `+` slice op, gmail/googlemail domain scope, `lastIndexOf('@')` usage, and the `.map(normalizeAdminEmail)` chain. Aggregator post-change: 2645 passed / 0 failed across 27 suites. Pushed to main 2026-04-22. (2026-04-22)
- [x] **`/api/auth/reset-password` 500-on-every-call в†’ fixed via self-healing schema bootstrap.** Root cause: Hostinger doesn't run `drizzle-kit push` on deploy, so the `password_reset_tokens` table that `0001_password_reset_tokens.sql` defines was never created on production MySQL. Every reset attempt threw `ER_NO_SUCH_TABLE` inside `consumePasswordResetToken` and the route catch surfaced a generic 500. Fix in `lib/password-reset.ts`: one-time-per-process `ensureSchema()` that runs `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS password_reset_tokens (...)` matching the migration byte-for-byte, called from the top of `mintPasswordResetToken` and `lookupPasswordResetToken`. Defence-in-depth: route now inspects `err.code === "ER_NO_SUCH_TABLE"` and returns 409 (same user-facing message as a stale/missing token) instead of 500. Bootstrap is marked `REMOVE WHEN MIGRATIONS RUN AT DEPLOY` so we don't leave runtime DDL in place forever. Local PDF-tool harness still 17/17 green; `tsc --noEmit` clean. (2026-04-20)
- [x] **`/account` в†’ `/app/settings` redirect shipped.** `/account` was 404'ing in prod despite being linked from the pricing-page BYOK CTA. Added `app/account/page.tsx` that `redirect("/app/settings")` at render вЂ” keeps external links working (email campaigns, marketing collateral) without duplicating the settings UI. `/app/settings` itself already auth-gates, so unauthed visitors get bounced to `/login` transitively. (2026-04-20)

- [x] **`/tool/pdf-to-office` runner shipped (user-reported defect: "not working").** Root cause: the URL returned 200 HTML, which is why `scripts/smoke-live.mjs` was passing, but the page was rendering `ComingSoonRunner` because `pdf-to-office` wasn't in the `LIVE_TOOL_IDS` set in `app/tool/[id]/page.tsx`. From an end-user's POV (including the reporter's screenshot), the disabled "Choose file / Use sample" buttons made the tool indistinguishable from broken. Fix: three new files shipped together вЂ” (1) `lib/tools-server/pdf-to-office.ts` converts extracted text to `.docx` (one heading per page, page-break between pages, Calibri 11pt, US Letter, OCR-candidate placeholder paragraphs) or `.txt` (UTF-8 with `\f` between pages); (2) `app/api/tools/pdf-to-office/route.ts` is the POST endpoint вЂ” Node runtime, 25 MB body cap, per-IP 10/min throttle, Zod format enum, status-code map (400 bad form / invalid PDF, 413 too large, 422 `no_extractable_text`, 429 rate-limited, 500 server error), Content-Disposition with RFC 5987 filename, `x-page-count` + `x-ocr-candidate-pages` response headers for the client UI; (3) `components/tools/PdfToOfficeTool.tsx` is the client runner вЂ” `ToolDropzone` + radio-card format selector (Word / Plain text) + ResultCard with download button + conditional OCR nudge + explicit v2-deferred note pointing tabular users to `/tool/ai-ocr`. Wired into `app/tool/[id]/page.tsx` switch, and that page now special-cases the reassurance row for server-side free tools so the "Stays in your browser" claim isn't a lie (new copy: "Your PDF is converted in-memory on our servers and discarded the moment the download completes вЂ” nothing is stored."). Server-side was the right call despite breaking the all-client-side free-tool pattern: pdfjs's worker needs bundling under a strict CSP and the `docx` library would bloat every visitor's bundle. No auth, no credit spend, no disk writes. `tsc --noEmit` clean, 17/17 existing PDF-tool harness still green. **Also extended `scripts/smoke-live.mjs`** with a new per-path assertion that live tool pages must NOT contain the string `TOOL RUNNER LANDS IN` вЂ” so any future regression where a runner is registered-but-disabled fails smoke instead of passing silently. Installed `docx@^9.6.1` as a runtime dep. (2026-04-20)
- [x] **`/api/tools/pdf-to-office` worker hotfix вЂ” real PDFs now round-trip end-to-end.** After the runner shipped, the page rendered correctly but the actual conversion 500'd in prod. SSH into Hostinger + tailing `~/domains/pdfcraftai.com/nodejs/console.log` revealed pdfjs's "fake worker" fallback was failing at runtime: `Setting up fake worker failed: "Cannot find module '.../pdfjs-dist/legacy/build/pdf.worker.mjs' imported from '.../pdfjs-dist/legacy/build/pdf.mjs'"`. Root cause: pdfjs's `pdf.mjs` does a *dynamic* import of `./pdf.worker.mjs` to spin up its in-process worker under Node, and that dynamic import is invisible to Next.js's standalone tracer вЂ” so the 2.3 MB worker file was never copied into `.next/standalone/node_modules/pdfjs-dist/legacy/build/`. Fix is two layers, both in this commit: **(1)** `next.config.mjs` adds `experimental.outputFileTracingIncludes` to force-copy `pdfjs-dist/legacy/build/pdf.worker.mjs` into the standalone bundle for every `/api/**/*` route вЂ” so pdfjs's default `./pdf.worker.mjs` lookup now resolves; **(2)** `lib/ai/pdf-extract.ts` adds an idempotent `ensureWorkerConfigured()` that runs on first call to `extractPdfText`, uses `createRequire(import.meta.url).resolve(...)` + `pathToFileURL(...)` to pin `GlobalWorkerOptions.workerSrc` to an explicit `file://` URL вЂ” belt-and-braces if a future Next version changes its tracing rules, and the idempotent flag means any latency hit only happens on the very first conversion in a worker's lifetime. Critically, the setter runs LAZILY inside the function (not at module load), because eagerly resolving at import-time breaks `next build`'s "Collecting page data" phase, which evaluates route modules in a webpack-bundled context where `require.resolve` against an ESM package fails before standalone tracing has even copied node_modules. Verified locally with a synthesized 3-page PDF round-tripped through the standalone bundle: `status=200`, `x-page-count=3`, 8.8 KB output, valid .docx ZIP whose `word/document.xml` contains all three pages of the input text. Also benefits `/api/ai/{chat,summarize,translate,compare,ocr}` вЂ” they share the same extractor and were silently latently broken too. **Verified LIVE on prod (commit `8271a61`, 2026-04-20 03:42 UTC):** same synthesized 3-page PDF POSTed to `https://pdfcraftai.com/api/tools/pdf-to-office` returned `status=200`, `x-page-count=3`, 8886-byte .docx, and the extracted `word/document.xml` contains all three pages of input text verbatim. Brief prod instability followed the deploy вЂ” LiteSpeed accumulated five stale `next-server` processes from prior deploys (02:59 / 03:13 / 03:31 / 03:32 / 03:39) which hit Node's thread-creation limit (`Assertion failed: (0) == (uv_thread_create(...))` in `stderr.log`) and 503'd the smoke harness; resolved via SSH `pkill -9 next-server` + `pkill -9 -f lsnode.js` so LiteSpeed could respawn one clean worker. Post-restart: `/api/health` ok=true db=31ms + full 54/54 `scripts/smoke-live.mjs` PASS + end-to-end PDF round-trip re-verified. (2026-04-20)

- [x] **`/tool/ai-sign` shipped end-to-end (fifth and final of 5 Phase 5.6 Coming-Soon tools вЂ” Phase 5.6 COMPLETE).** Commit `5e85ca0` (2026-04-20). Three new files + one edited wire-up: (1) `lib/ai/sign.ts` вЂ” ~700-line orchestrator. Exports `SignFieldKey` (`"__signature" | "__initials" | "__skip" | "fullName" | "initials" | "email" | "phone" | "date" | "company" | "title" | "address" | \`custom:${string}\``), `SignUserInfo` (fullName required; all other fields optional string; customFields capped at 20 k/v pairs), `SignInput`, `SignFilling`, `SignUnfilled`, `SignResult`, `NoAIProviderConfiguredError`, `SignParseError`, `signPdf()`. Four-stage pipeline: (1) positioned pdfjs extraction via the in-house path (matches ai-redact's approach вЂ” returns `pages[{ items[{x,y,w,h,str}], combined, charMap }]` + `ocrCandidatePages` + `fullText`), (2) strict JSON envelope prompt at temperature 0.1 asking for `{ fills: [{ label, anchorText, fieldKey, page, reason }] }` with `postProcessJson` fence stripping + dedicated `SignParseError` class, (3) whitespace-tolerant substring matching per fill вЂ” compress `haystack + needle` to lowercased no-whitespace and `indexOf` the anchor, map endpoints back to original item indices, (4) pdf-lib `drawText` placed right-of-anchor baseline with binary-search shrink-to-fit + ellipsize (never overflows the anchor's right-margin). Font rules: special keys `__signature` + `__initials` use `StandardFonts.HelveticaBoldOblique` at 16pt in dark blue `rgb(0.04, 0.07, 0.42)`; all other keys use `StandardFonts.Helvetica` at 10pt black. `__skip` no-ops (model flagged that a label isn't actually a field). `custom:<slug>` resolves against the `customFields` bundle; unknown slugs surface as `unmatched[]`. `normalizeUserInfo()` builds a `valueByKey` Map + `availableKeys` list that's injected into the model prompt so it knows which fields it CAN fill (AI hallucination guard). Returns `{ pdfBytes, signedPdfFilename, markdown, fillings[], unmatched[], pageCount, ocrCandidatePages, providerId, model, usage, wasTruncated }`; markdown summary lists each filled field with page + anchor + reason, unmatched anchors at the bottom, and the explicit non-crypto caveat. (2) `app/api/ai/sign/route.ts` вЂ” 429-line, 8-step pipeline mirroring `/api/ai/redact/route.ts` (auth в†’ parseMultipart (pdf + info JSON + idempotencyKey) в†’ validate PDF в‰¤25 MB + info в‰¤16 KB (413 `info_too_large`) в†’ `parseUserInfo()` validator (fullName non-empty required; well-known optional fields must be string if present; customFields max 20 {key, value} pairs with empty pairs filtered out) в†’ idempotency replay (kind `"signing"` вЂ” returns `signedPdfBase64: null` with flag, client shows "Re-run for a fresh PDF") в†’ `spendCredits(10)` with spend-key `ai:sign:<idempotencyKey>` в†’ `signPdf()` в†’ zero-findings-with->=90%-OCR-pages guard (422 `no_extractable_text` + refund) в†’ `db.transaction` insert files row (filename `"${base} вЂ” Fill & Sign Report.md"`) + ai_outputs row with `kind: "signing"` + meta `{ fillings[], unmatched[], signedPdfFilename, pageCount, ocrCandidatePages, providerId, model, tokensIn, tokensOut, wasTruncated, creditCost }`). Route error map: `NoAIProviderConfiguredError` -> 503 no_ai_provider_configured; `SignParseError` -> 502 `sign_parse_failed` + refund; `pdf-extract` failures -> 400 `pdf_extract_failed`; generic -> 502 `sign_failed` + refund. 207 persist-failed fallback still returns the base64 PDF + markdown so nothing the user paid for is lost. TS2352 fix at line 401: `(out as unknown as Record<string, string>)[k] = trimmed;` вЂ” needed the `unknown` cast bridge because `SignUserInfo` and `Record<string, string>` don't sufficiently overlap for a direct cast. (3) `components/tools/SignPdfTool.tsx` вЂ” `"use client"` runner with the standard auth gate (`useSession()` render-time + `getSession()` defense-in-depth probe, `SIGN_IN_HREF = "/login?callbackUrl=" + encodeURIComponent("/tool/ai-sign")`). State: file, fullName (required, trim-checked for `canSubmit`), initials, email, phone, date (defaults to `todayIso()` = today's YYYY-MM-DD UTC), company, title, address, customFields[{key, value}] array. UI: `ToolDropzone` (PDF, в‰¤25 MB) + personal-details grid (`repeat(auto-fit, minmax(220px, 1fr))`) + custom-fields table with Add Row / Remove Row controls (capped at 20) + amber-bordered "Not a cryptographic signature" caveat card directing legally-binding needs to DocuSign / Adobe Sign. POST multipart to `/api/ai/sign` with `pdf` + `info` (JSON.stringified bundle) + `idempotencyKey` (crypto.randomUUID). `DownloadSignedButton` decodes `atob(pdfBase64) -> Uint8Array -> Blob("application/pdf") -> anchor click -> URL.revokeObjectURL`. Button labels: "Fill & sign вЂ” 10 credits" (authed) / "Sign in to fill & sign" (anon) / "FillingвЂ¦" (busy). `mapErrorBody()` covers 401/402/409/413 (with `info_too_large` branch)/422/400/502 (with `sign_parse_failed` branch)/503. ResultCard surfaces fill count, per-page provenance, markdown summary, and the non-crypto caveat badge. (4) Wire-up in `app/tool/[id]/page.tsx` вЂ” added `"ai-sign"` to `LIVE_TOOL_IDS`, imported `SignPdfTool`, added `case "ai-sign":` branch to the ToolRunner switch, updated the phase-comment header to list all 5 Phase 5.6 tools (AI В· Rewrite, AI В· Table, AI В· Redact, AI В· Generate, AI В· Sign). No new migration needed вЂ” `0003_extend_ai_output_kinds.sql` (from the ai-rewrite ship) already covers the `"signing"` enum value. **Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` exit 0 (after the TS2352 unknown-cast fix); pushed `7e0818d..5e85ca0  main -> main`; live prod probes after Hostinger redeploy all green вЂ” `GET https://pdfcraftai.com/tool/ai-sign` 200 with "Fill & sign вЂ” 10 credits" button + "Drop a PDF to fill & sign" dropzone rendered, `GET https://pdfcraftai.com/api/ai/sign` 405 (POST-only), `POST https://pdfcraftai.com/api/ai/sign` with anon JSON body 401 `{"error":"not_authenticated"}`, `POST https://pdfcraftai.com/api/ai/sign` with anon multipart 401 `{"error":"not_authenticated"}` (auth gate is first in the pipeline, so info validation doesn't leak). Comparison probes confirmed all four Phase 5.6 AI routes (`sign` / `redact` / `generate` / `table`) return 405 on GET вЂ” consistent route registration across the whole phase. **Phase 5.6 Coming-Soon set now empty вЂ” all five tools (rewrite / table / redact / generate / sign) shipped end-to-end.** (2026-04-20)
- [x] **`/tool/ai-generate` shipped end-to-end (fourth of 5 Phase 5.6 Coming-Soon tools).** Commit `d00ee8a` (2026-04-20). Three new files + one edited wire-up: (1) `lib/ai/generate.ts` вЂ” ~620-line helper implementing a two-stage promptв†’PDF pipeline. Exports `GenerateDocType` (`"memo" | "report" | "brief" | "letter" | "blog" | "outline" | "other"`), `GenerateLength` (`"short" | "medium" | "long"`), `GenerateTone` (`"neutral" | "formal" | "casual" | "technical"`), `generatePdf()`, `NoAIProviderConfiguredError`. Stage 1: builds a system prompt per doc type + length + tone, asks the model for clean markdown at temperature 0.4 with a `PROMPT_CHAR_BUDGET = 8,000` input clamp and per-length `MAX_TOKENS_BY_LENGTH` output cap (short 900 / medium 2200 / long 4600); extracts stop-reason for `wasTruncated` detection (`"max_tokens"` or `"length"`). Stage 2: custom markdown renderer on top of `pdf-lib` вЂ” `parseMarkdown()` regex-splits blocks into `h1` / `h2` / `h3` / `para` / `ulist` / `olist` / `hr`, `parseInline()` tracks bold/italic spans with `hasClosingMarker()` lookahead (unterminated markers fall through as literals). Layout: US-Letter 612Г—792pt with 72pt (1") margins (468pt content width), `drawHeading()` at 24/18/14pt with gap-before/after, `drawParagraph()` at 11pt with 16pt line height, `drawList()` with bullet indent 14 / text indent 28, `drawHr()` with a 0.5pt rule. Pagination via `ensureSpace(ctx, needed)` which adds a fresh page when `cursorY - needed < marginY`. `ensureLeadingH1()` prepends the title as an H1 if the markdown doesn't already start with `# `. Uses the Helvetica family (Helvetica / Bold / Oblique / BoldOblique) from `StandardFonts` so no font files ship. Word-wrap preserves inline spans across line breaks (including bold-italic combos via independent flag toggles). (2) `app/api/ai/generate/route.ts` вЂ” ~290 lines, 8-step pipeline (auth в†’ parseBody (JSON **or** multipart вЂ” no PDF upload for this tool) в†’ validate prompt (16,000 char max в†’ 413 `prompt_too_long` with `maxChars`) + docType + length + tone в†’ idempotency replay в†’ spendCredits(20) `ai:generate:<key>` в†’ generatePdf в†’ `db.transaction` insert files + ai_outputs with `kind: "generation"` + meta `{ promptChars, title, docType, length, tone, pageCount, pdfFilename, providerId, model, tokensIn, tokensOut, wasTruncated, creditCost }`). Response carries the generated PDF as **base64** (we don't persist PDF bytes; only the summary markdown lands in `ai_outputs.content_md`, filename `"${title} вЂ” Generated.md"`). Refunds on `NoAIProviderConfiguredError` в†’ 503, generic failure в†’ 502 `generate_failed`. Replay branch returns `pdfBase64: null` (bytes aren't persisted; client surfaces "Re-run for a fresh PDF" copy). 207 persist-failed fallback still hands back the base64 PDF + markdown so the user's 20-credit spend isn't lost. `derivePdfFilename(title)` strips `\/:"*?<>|`, caps at 80 chars, appends `.pdf`. (3) `components/tools/GeneratePdfTool.tsx` вЂ” ~530 lines. `"use client"` with the same auth gate pattern as ai-rewrite / ai-table / ai-redact (`useSession()` render-time + `getSession()` defense-in-depth probe; `SIGN_IN_HREF = "/login?callbackUrl=" + encodeURIComponent("/tool/ai-generate")`). Form fields: optional title (120-char max), required prompt textarea with a live char counter against 16,000, three selects (Format / Length / Tone). POSTs JSON (not multipart) to `/api/ai/generate`. Button labels: "Generate PDF вЂ” 20 credits" (authed) / "Sign in to generate" (anon) / "GeneratingвЂ¦" (busy). `DownloadPdfButton` decodes `atob(pdfBase64) в†’ Uint8Array в†’ Blob("application/pdf") в†’ anchor click в†’ URL.revokeObjectURL` to trigger the download. ResultCard renders Generate icon header, provider/model/pageCount/truncation-chip provenance footer, replay-aware copy when `pdfBase64 === null && replay === true`. `mapErrorBody()` covers 401/402/409/413 (with `prompt_too_long` branch returning `maxChars`)/400/502/503. - [x] **`/tool/ai-redact` shipped end-to-end (third of 5 Phase 5.6 Coming-Soon tools).** Commit `77278b1` (2026-04-20). Three new files + one edited wire-up: (1) `lib/ai/redact.ts` вЂ” ~600-line helper. Because `extractPdfText` strips positions, this file re-does pdfjs extraction in-house via `pdfjs-dist/legacy` + a `createRequire` worker bootstrap, returning `{ pageCount, pages[{ items[{x,y,w,h,str}], combined, charMap }], fullText, ocrCandidatePages }`. The model is asked for a strict JSON envelope `{ findings: [{ category, text, reason }] }` across 12 PII categories (`EMAIL` / `PHONE` / `SSN` / `CREDIT_CARD` / `ADDRESS` / `PERSON_NAME` / `DATE_OF_BIRTH` / `PASSPORT` / `DRIVER_LICENSE` / `IP_ADDRESS` / `API_KEY` / `BANK_ACCOUNT` / `OTHER`) at temperature 0.1; parsing mirrors `lib/ai/table.ts` with a dedicated `RedactParseError` class. For each finding we do whitespace-tolerant substring matching (compress `haystack + needle` to lowercased no-whitespace, run `indexOf`, map endpoints back to original item indices) so a name split by pdfjs into `["John ", "Smith"]` still matches. Every spanned item gets a `pdf-lib` `page.drawRectangle({ color: rgb(0,0,0) })` with В±2px descender padding. Returns `{ pdfBytes, redactedPdfFilename, markdown, findings[], unmatched[], pageCount, ocrCandidatePages, providerId, model, usage, wasTruncated }`; markdown summary includes by-category counts + per-finding table + unmatched table + **explicit security caveat** that this is a visual overlay, the underlying content-stream text is untouched, and print-to-PDF is required for sensitive handoffs. 240k input char budget; 2400 output token cap. Refunds on `NoAIProviderConfiguredError` в†’ 503, `RedactParseError` в†’ 502 `redact_parse_failed`, extract failures в†’ 400 `pdf_extract_failed`, generic в†’ 502 `redact_failed`. Special case: if the pipeline succeeded with zero findings AND в‰Ґ90% of pages were flagged as OCR-candidates, treat as `no_extractable_text` в†’ 422 + refund. Replays return `redactedPdfBase64: null` with a flag вЂ” the client shows "Re-run for a fresh PDF" because only the summary is persisted. 207 fallback on persist-failure still hands back the base64 PDF. (3) `components/tools/RedactPdfTool.tsx` вЂ” `"use client"` with the same auth gate pattern (`useSession()` render-time + `getSession()` defense-in-depth probe). `DownloadRedactedButton` converts `atob(base64) в†’ Uint8Array в†’ Blob в†’ anchor click` to trigger the download. Dropzone prompt: "Drop a PDF to redact"; button label: "Redact PDF вЂ” 5 credits". ### Password reset redemption flow (end-to-end)

- [x] **Password reset-link redemption shipped end-to-end.** Completes the forgot-password в†’ email-link в†’ new-password loop that was previously stubbed.
  - **Schema (`db/schema/auth.ts`)** вЂ” new `password_reset_tokens` table: `id` (uuid), `user_id` (FK в†’ `users.id` ON DELETE cascade), `token_hash` (sha256-hex, unique), `expires_at` (ts(3)), `consumed_at` (ts(3), nullable), `created_at` (ts(3), default now). Two indexes: `user_id`, `expires_at`.
  - **Migration (`db/migrations/0001_password_reset_tokens.sql` + `meta/_journal.json`)** вЂ” drizzle-kit format, statement-breakpoint-separated, journaled so `pnpm db:push` / `pnpm db:generate` pick it up; also runnable directly via `mysql` CLI on Hostinger as a manual fallback.
  - **Helper (`lib/password-reset.ts`)** вЂ” `mintPasswordResetToken(email)` (silent no-op on unknown email, 32-byte random hex raw token, 30-minute TTL, stores only sha256 hash at rest), `lookupPasswordResetToken(raw)` (cheap-rejects non-64-hex before any DB hit), `consumePasswordResetToken(raw, newPassword)` (race-safe single-use via guarded `UPDATE ... WHERE id=? AND consumed_at IS NULL`, bcrypt-10 the new password, then invalidates sibling outstanding tokens for the same user so reset-twice can't leave a live second link).
  - **Forgot endpoint (`app/api/auth/forgot-password/route.ts`)** вЂ” rewritten: still anti-enumeration 200 on valid payload, still 1/min per-email rate-limited; now mints the token and logs the full reset URL + email + expiry to the Node process log (Hostinger tail) until a transactional mail provider is wired. `NEXT_PUBLIC_SITE_URL` override respected; falls back to the request origin.
  - **Reset endpoint (`app/api/auth/reset-password/route.ts`)** вЂ” new POST. Zod validates 64-hex token + 8вЂ“128-char password. Per-IP bucket rate limit (5/min) before the DB. Returns 200 on success, 400 on bad payload, 409 on expired/consumed/missing, 429 on rate limit, 500 on DB error. Same "invalid or expired" message for 409 variants (enumeration-safe).
  - **Dynamic page (`app/reset-password/[token]/page.tsx`)** вЂ” async server component, `dynamic = "force-dynamic"`, verifies token server-side on mount. Invalid в†’ renders `AuthShell` with "This reset link won't work" + `<I.Info>` warning card + CTA back to `/forgot-password`. Valid в†’ renders `<ResetPasswordForm token=... />` under "Choose a new password".
  - **Client form (`components/auth/ResetPasswordForm.tsx`)** вЂ” twin `PasswordField`s (new + confirm) with show/hide toggles, live `PasswordStrength` indicator, disabled-until (length в‰Ґ 8, matches confirm, strength в‰Ґ 2), inline errors, `router.replace("/login?reset=1")` on 200 (replace, not push вЂ” keeps the reset URL out of history).
  - **Middleware (`auth.config.ts`)** вЂ” `/reset-password/<token>` added to the "auth page" redirect guard so already-signed-in users bounce to `/app/dashboard` instead of redeeming a token they don't need.
  - **Login flash (`components/auth/LoginForm.tsx`)** вЂ” `useSearchParams` reads `?reset=1`; shows a green `<I.Check>` banner ("Password updated. Sign in with your new password to continue.") above the Google SSO button.
  - **Typechecked clean** (`./node_modules/.bin/tsc --noEmit` в†’ `EXIT=0`). Swapping in Resend/Postmark once the mailbox is live is a single drop-in around the `console.log` in the forgot endpoint. (2026-04-20)

- [x] **Task #27 Phase E CLOSED вЂ” annual-prepay tier + INR pricing + promo codes.** (2026-04-22) Commit `1b33b21` pushed to main. 18 files changed / +4,278 / в€’248. Closes the last Phase E pricing lever on the Net Margin Roadmap: a single bundle that adds (a) annual-prepay as a pack variant (12Г— credits at 20% off, gated by `ANNUAL_MONTHS=12` + `ANNUAL_DISCOUNT_BPS=2000` in `lib/pricing.ts`; new `packCreditsForVariant(pack, variant)` returns `pack.credits * 12` on annual, baseline on monthly; rail-aware `packAmountMinor(pack, variant, rail)` respects the annual discount on both USD cents + INR paise), (b) per-pack INR pricing surfaced on the Razorpay rail (Starter в‚№399, Creator в‚№1499, Pro в‚№4999, Studio в‚№12499) via optional `inrPrice` on every pack + threaded through the geo-router, and (c) first-class promo-code support with an 8-gate validator (`isActive в†’ startsAt в†’ expiresAt в†’ currency в†’ packIds в†’ annualOnly в†’ maxRedemptions в†’ perUserLimit`), three discount kinds (`percent` bps off subtotal, `flat` micros off clamped at subtotal, `bonus_credits` extra credits post-capture), and an admin tool at `/admin/promos` to mint/disable codes. Bundle: (a) **Migration 0015** вЂ” `db/migrations/0015_promo_codes_and_annual.sql`. Additive-only. New tables `promo_codes` + `promo_redemptions`; new nullable columns on `payments` (`promo_code_id varchar(36)`, `promo_discount_micros bigint`, `promo_bonus_credits int`, `annual_variant tinyint(1)`). `currency char(3) NULL` on both promo tables. Composite index `promo_redemptions(promo_code_id, user_id)` backs the per-user-limit gate. FK strategy: RESTRICT on `promo_redemptions.promo_code_id` (don't orphan audit rows), CASCADE on `payment_id` (ledger is source of truth), SET NULL on `payments.promo_code_id` (deleting a code doesn't drop the payment). **DEPLOY ORDER:** pipe to Hostinger MySQL BEFORE activating the admin mint form вЂ” app is safe without the migration (promo input + annual toggle refuse gracefully when the new columns are absent from the ledger read path) but the inventory query + mint path require the tables to exist. (c) **Pricing surface** вЂ” `lib/pricing.ts` new constants `ANNUAL_MONTHS=12` + `ANNUAL_DISCOUNT_BPS=2000`; every pack gains optional `inrPrice`; `packCreditsForVariant(pack, variant)` returns 12Г— credits on annual branch; rail-aware `packAmountMinor(pack, variant, rail)` respects annual discount on both rails (refactored from legacy `pack.price * 100` to `basePrice = pack.price` + `Math.round(basePrice * 100)` so the discount branch reads cleanly вЂ” test-dual-rail-routing C6 relaxed to accept either pattern). (d) **Resolver** вЂ” `lib/promos/resolver.ts` (426 lines). Pure function `resolvePromo({code, userId, pack, variant, currency, rail, now}) в†’ { ok: true, ... } | { ok: false, reason }` with 9 reason enums. Gates run in order; first failure short-circuits. `percent` kind returns bps off subtotal (stored computed-only in `promoDiscountMicros` at capture time вЂ” `promo_discount_bps` is NOT persisted); `flat` returns micros off clamped at subtotal (never negative); `bonus_credits` returns extra credits to grant post-capture. (e) **Server actions** вЂ” `lib/promos/actions.ts` (566 lines). `adminCreatePromoCodeAction` + `adminDisablePromoCodeAction` gated by `requireAdmin()`; `applyPromoToCheckoutAction` is user-scoped via `auth()`. Invariants guarded: can't apply a promo twice to the same payment; annual-only promos reject monthly variant; flat discount clamps at subtotal. (g) **Ledger wiring** вЂ” `lib/payments/ledger.ts` populates `promo_discount_micros` / `promo_bonus_credits` / `annual_variant` from the payment row on webhook finalization. `String(fin.fxRateUsed)` stays the only `Number()`-free persistence path вЂ” this commit does NOT regress the credit-ledger-financials C6 invariant. - [x] **Task #26 Phase E CLOSED вЂ” prompt version registry + A/B testing infra.** (2026-04-22) Commit `941dac6` pushed to main. 13 files changed / +2,329 / в€’0. Layers a prompt-variant registry on top of the Phase A1 `ai_usage` audit table so (a) every AI call records which prompt variant it executed under, (b) traffic can be weighted-split across variants deterministically per user via djb2-hashed bucketing, and (c) the new `/admin/prompts` page surfaces per-variant infra metrics for "ship if healthier, revert if worse" decisions. Bundle: (a) **Migration 0014** вЂ” `db/migrations/0014_ai_usage_prompt_version.sql` вЂ” additive ALTER adding `prompt_version varchar(32) NULL` + `experiment_id varchar(64) NULL` to `ai_usage` AFTER `response_truncated`, no DEFAULT / no index / no DROP (low-cardinality; GROUP BY on 7вЂ“30d windows is fine live). **DEPLOY ORDER:** must pipe to Hostinger MySQL BEFORE the code ships; the write-path populates both columns unconditionally. (b) **Schema parity** вЂ” `db/schema/app.ts` mirrors both columns at matching widths. (c) **Write path** вЂ” `lib/ai/usage.ts` `RecordAiUsageInput` gains `promptVersion` / `experimentId` (both `string | null`); persistence clamps to 32/64 chars to defend against oversize payloads. (d) **Registry module** вЂ” `lib/ai/prompts/registry.ts` (~530 lines). `PROMPT_REGISTRY: Record<PromptOp, PromptVersion[]>` covers all 10 `AIOp` entries; `EXPERIMENTS = []` at ship (deterministic `"v1"` at 100% for every op). `resolvePromptVersion(op, seed)` returns `{version, experimentId}`: single-enabled-variant op returns that id + `experimentId=null`; 2+ enabled variants with a registered `Experiment` returns weighted-random assignment via `stableHashToBps(op:seed)` (djb2 `h = (h << 5) + h + c` folded into `(h >>> 0) % 10000` bps space) + the matching `experimentId`; 2+ enabled variants with NO `Experiment` still assigns by weight but returns `experimentId=null` вЂ” "misconfigured but safe", the admin page surfaces this as a red banner. `classifyOpState` classifies each op into `single | experiment | misconfigured | empty`. `RECORDING_ENABLED` kill switch nulls returned audit strings at call-sites without rolling back the migration. `__PROMPT_REGISTRY_INTERNALS` test hook exports the internals. (e) **Summarize wire-up** вЂ” `lib/ai/summarize.ts`. `SummarizeInput` gains `userId` (passed through from the route's `auth()`); `SummarizeResult` + `BatchPlan` + `BatchResult` all carry `promptVersion` + `experimentId`. `buildSystemPrompt(opts)` gains `promptVersion: string` as the documented extensibility point вЂ” v1 is the only registered variant today and any other id fallbacks to v1 behavior (registry + renderer must move together). Both success and error `recordAiUsage()` call-sites in `/api/ai/summarize` thread the audit pair. (f) **Batch timing** вЂ” `/api/ai/batch/submit` captures resolved variant into `opPayload` at plan time; `/api/ai/batch/[jobId]` reads back with `?? null` legacy fallback so pre-0014 batches submitted before this code shipped don't throw, and passes through to both `finalizeSummarizeBatchResult` + the finalize-time `recordAiUsage({batchMode: true, ...})` so the audit row reflects the variant the batch ACTUALLY executed under (not what the registry would pick now if reweighted mid-flight). (g) **/admin/prompts page** вЂ” `app/admin/prompts/page.tsx` (~400 lines). `force-dynamic` + `nodejs` runtime + default export; consumes `PROMPT_REGISTRY` + `classifyOpState` + `getPromptVersionRollout`. Red banner on any op in `misconfigured` state; yellow banner when `RECORDING_ENABLED=false`. 4-card stat strip (registered variants / active experiments / version coverage N d / misconfigured ops) + registry table + per-op state table + traffic split table + active experiments table. `DayPicker` base=`/admin/prompts` with `ErrorBanner` fallback on query failure. NAV entry registered in `app/admin/layout.tsx` under Ops. (h) **Admin query helper** вЂ” `lib/admin/phase-e-queries.ts` (~195 lines). `PhaseEQueryResult<T>` envelope mirrors `PhaseDQueryResult` / `AdminQueryResult`; `server-only` pin. `getPromptVersionRollout({days})` groups `ai_usage` by `(operation, prompt_version, experiment_id)` over a clamped 1вЂ“90d window with rollup filter `WHERE prompt_version IS NOT NULL` so pre-0014 rows don't skew per-variant percentages (matches the convention from `response_truncated` / `cached_input_tokens`). Returns `totalCalls` + `totalCallsWithVersion` so the page shows version-coverage % (operator cue when code ship hasn't propagated). The 10th tool (`PdfToOfficeTool`) is correctly out of scope вЂ” it hits the deterministic `/api/tools/pdf-to-office` converter, not `/api/ai/*`. Same part-2 commit added `lib/payments/dunning.ts` вЂ” Phase-E-ready state-machine scaffold for subscription lifecycle: four states (`current` в†’ `past_due` в†’ `suspended` в†’ `cancelled`), three event kinds (`payment_failed`, `payment_succeeded`, `subscription_cancelled`), `DUNNING_POLICY` constants (3-day grace past-due, 7-day suspended-before-cancel), a pure idempotent `applyDunningEvent` reducer keyed on `providerEventId`, and `isEntitled` guard (today: `current` + `past_due` entitled; `suspended` + `cancelled` not). The module intentionally does NOT touch the DB вЂ” it's imported-but-dormant until Phase E wires the `subscription_dunning` table + webhook handlers for Paddle `subscription.payment_failed/succeeded/canceled` and Razorpay `subscription.charged/pending/halted/cancelled`. Self-serve refund UI remains the only unstarted half of Task #22 вЂ” deferred to Phase E because today's ledger is one-shot credits (refund = full reversal, already handled by the webhook dispute path), whereas self-serve partial refunds only become meaningful once recurring plans ship. - [x] **Task #23 Phase D CLOSED вЂ” receipt/invoice generator + GSTIN config (PART 1 + PART 2).** (2026-04-22) Shipped in two bundles on main. **PART 1** landed earlier on 2026-04-22 with the pdf-lib A4 renderer (`lib/invoicing/renderer.ts`), the GSTIN Mod-36 CBIC checksum validator (`lib/invoicing/gstin.ts`, `INDIAN_STATE_CODES` 38-entry lookup), the classifier (`lib/invoicing/classify.ts` в†’ `intra_state` / `inter_state` / `export` / `reverse_charge`), the deterministic invoice-number derivator (`lib/invoicing/types.ts` в†’ `deriveInvoiceNumber` returns `INV-{FY}-{8HEX}` with Apr 1 FY cutover), the env-driven seller identity loader (`lib/invoicing/seller.ts` reading `INVOICE_SELLER_*` with `"GSTIN: pending registration"` fallback until CA-owned registration lands), the assembler (`lib/invoicing/assemble.ts` в†’ `assembleInvoiceInput({ payment, ledger, buyer, seller, notes })`), and the GET handler at `/api/invoices/[paymentId]` that gates on owner-only access (404 not 403 on mismatched userId so we don't leak row existence, 409 `payment_not_captured` on pending/failed/cancelled) and streams `Content-Type: application/pdf` + `Content-Disposition: attachment; filename="invoice-INV-YYYY-XXXXXXXX.pdf"`. **PART 2** landed as commit `2ab2dd3` (9 files / +1,457 / в€’20): the buyer-side billing form that feeds the PART 1 assembler. No DEFAULT, no NOT NULL, no index (low-cardinality; joined only on the owner-gated invoice route, not scanned). (b) **Schema parity** вЂ” `db/schema/auth.ts` mirrors all 8 columns via Drizzle `varchar(...)` declarations at exact widths. Zod pipeline uses `.trim().transform((v) => (v.length > 0 ? v : null)).nullable().default(null)` on every field so a blank submission clears the row without a second null-check branch. GSTIN validation delegates to `validateGstin` from `lib/invoicing/gstin` and maps all 6 failure reasons (`format_invalid`, `length_invalid`, `checksum_invalid`, `state_code_invalid`, `entity_code_invalid`, `default_char_invalid`) to user-facing copy. Buyer state is validated against `INDIAN_STATE_CODES` and silently dropped if not in the known set. Name prefers `user.billingName || user.name` (the former is the legal entity for B2B receipts; the latter is a display name). Address lines are assembled from line1 / line2 / `city, PIN` / state name / country code вЂ” NULL / empty values are skipped so the renderer doesn't print blank rows. NAV entry registered in `app/admin/layout.tsx` under Money (rationale: "can buyers download a compliant receipt?" is a money-flow question вЂ” failed invoice download = buyer escalates to support = refund risk). An "Invoice header logic" card enumerates the three-state title logic (`Receipt` / `Tax Invoice` / `Export Invoice`) so an operator can confirm at a glance which state we're in today (Receipt, pending GSTIN). - [x] **Admin margin dashboard endpoint shipped вЂ” Task #22 read-side / Phase A4 consumer surface.** Closes the last code gap on Task #22: the `ai_daily_margin` rollup table has been written nightly since the cron landed, but until now there was no read path вЂ” ops had to SSH + raw-SQL every time they wanted to see the 7-day streak. New `app/api/admin/margin/route.ts` (86 lines) is the GET-only authenticated endpoint: `await auth()` resolves the NextAuth session в†’ 401 `not_authenticated` on anonymous в†’ `isAdminEmail(email, process.env.ADMIN_EMAILS)` в†’ 403 `forbidden` on non-admin (403 not 404 so the UI can distinguish signed-in-as-non-admin from unknown endpoint) в†’ `clampAdminDays(url.searchParams.get("days"))` в†’ `getAdminMarginSummary({ days })` в†’ 200 JSON, 502 `rollup_read_failed` on DB error (matches `/api/ai/*` upstream-error posture). `force-dynamic` + `nodejs` runtime because Drizzle+mysql2 are node-only and "yesterday UTC" would freeze at build time under static rendering. **lib/ai/margin-rollup.ts** gained ~260 lines of admin surface: constants `ADMIN_MARGIN_MAX_DAYS = 90` (one quarter ceiling, matches `computeGreenStreak` maxDays) + `ADMIN_MARGIN_DEFAULT_DAYS = 14` (enough to visually confirm the 7-day streak); pure helpers `clampAdminDays(raw)` bounds [1,90] + default 14 on null/empty/non-integer, `parseAdminEmails(raw)` comma-splits + trims + lowercases + filters entries without `@`, with founder-email fallback (`rajasekarjavaee@gmail.com`) on empty/unset env so a fresh deploy doesn't lock admin out, `isAdminEmail(email, raw)` returns false on null/undefined email otherwise delegates to `parseAdminEmails(raw).has(email.toLowerCase())`; types `AdminMarginDaySummary` (per-day counts + min/max margin_bps + cost/revenue sums + allGreen boolean), `AdminMarginRedSlice` (flat row mirroring ai_daily_margin minus bookkeeping cols), `AdminMarginSummary` (generatedAt + range + currentStreakDays + gate7Reached + days[] + recentRedSlices[] + floorBpsByOp); and the main async `getAdminMarginSummary({ days, redSliceLimit })` вЂ” one GROUP BY per-day aggregate query (COUNT, SUM(CASE is_green=1), SUM(CASE is_green=0), MIN/MAX marginBps, SUM cost/revenue) + one ORDER BY desc LIMIT red-slices query (`eq(isGreen, 0)` filter вЂ” NOT `marginBps < floorBps` вЂ” so the admin view and the cron agree on what "red" means), + call to existing `computeGreenStreak({ throughDate })`. Window semantics: `days=14` means the 14 calendar days ending yesterday UTC (same day range the cron would have written), matching `lt(date, dayAfterYesterday)` bound so yesterday itself is inclusive. redSliceLimit clamped to [1, 50] вЂ” unbounded LIMIT on a composite-indexed scan can still hit unplanned rows. **Auth design note:** deliberately NOT using the cron's `x-cron-secret` shared-secret pattern вЂ” the cron runs headlessly so a secret works; this endpoint backs a human-facing dashboard so a logged-in Google session + email allowlist is the right model and piggy-backs on NextAuth which is already deployed.
